href="http://jkrowling.com">jkrowling<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Joanne  Rowling</b>, <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Companion_of_Honour" class="mw-redirect" title="Companion of Honour">CH</a>,&#32;<a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">OBE</a>,&#32;<a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society_of_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellow of the Royal Society of Literature">FRSL</a>,&#32;<a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_College_of_Physicians_of_Edinburgh" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellow of the Royal College of Physicians of Edinburgh">FRCPE</a></span> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xc5\x8b/: &#39;ng&#39; in &#39;sing&#39;">\xc5\x8b</span></span>/</a></span></span> "rolling";<sup id="cite_ref-bio_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> born 31 July 1965), writing under the pen names <b>J. K. Rowling</b> and <b>Robert Galbraith</b>, is a British <a href="/wiki/Novelist" title="Novelist">novelist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philanthropist" class="mw-redirect" title="Philanthropist">philanthropist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Film_producer" title="Film producer">film producer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television_producer" title="Television producer">television producer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Screenwriter" title="Screenwriter">screenwriter</a>, best known for writing the <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></i> fantasy series. The books have won multiple awards, and sold more than 500&#160;million copies,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_books" title="List of best-selling books">best-selling book series in history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> They have also been the basis for <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">a film series</a>, over which Rowling had overall approval on the scripts<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and was a producer on the final films in the series.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Yate" title="Yate">Yate</a>, Gloucestershire, England, Rowling was working as a researcher and bilingual secretary for <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> when she conceived the idea for the <i>Harry Potter</i> series while on a delayed train from <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> to London in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-WizardBehindPotter_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WizardBehindPotter-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The seven-year period that followed saw the death of her mother, birth of her first child, divorce from her first husband and relative poverty until the <a href="/wiki/Debut_novel" title="Debut novel">first novel</a> in the series, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone">Harry Potter and the Philosopher\'s Stone</a></i>, was published in 1997. There were six sequels, of which the last, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>, was released in 2007. Since then, Rowling has written five books for adult readers: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Casual_Vacancy" title="The Casual Vacancy">The Casual Vacancy</a></i> (2012) and\xe2\x80\x94under the <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonym</a> Robert Galbraith\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Crime_fiction" title="Crime fiction">crime fiction</a> novels <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cuckoo%27s_Calling" title="The Cuckoo&#39;s Calling">The Cuckoo\'s Calling</a></i> (2013), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silkworm" title="The Silkworm">The Silkworm</a></i> (2014), <i><a href="/wiki/Career_of_Evil" title="Career of Evil">Career of Evil</a></i> (2015), and <i><a href="/wiki/Lethal_White_(novel)" title="Lethal White (novel)">Lethal White</a></i> (2018).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling has lived a "<a href="/wiki/Rags_to_riches" title="Rags to riches">rags to riches</a>" life story, in which she progressed from living on state benefits to being the world\'s first billionaire author.<sup id="cite_ref-The_world&#39;s_first_billionaire_author_is_cashing_in_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_world&#39;s_first_billionaire_author_is_cashing_in-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> She lost her billionaire status after giving away much of her earnings to charity, but remains one of the wealthiest people in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-J.K._Rowling_Is_No_Longer_A_Billionaire,_Booted_Off_Forbes_List_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J.K._Rowling_Is_No_Longer_A_Billionaire,_Booted_Off_Forbes_List-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She is the United Kingdom\'s bestselling living author, with sales in excess of \xc2\xa3238M.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The 2016 <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Sunday Times Rich List</a></i> estimated Rowling\'s fortune at \xc2\xa3600&#160;million, ranking her as the joint 197th richest person in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-richlist_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richlist-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i></a> named her a runner-up for its 2007 <a href="/wiki/Time_Person_of_the_Year" title="Time Person of the Year">Person of the Year</a>, noting the social, moral, and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Harry_Potter" title="Politics of Harry Potter">political inspiration</a> she has given <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_fandom" title="Harry Potter fandom">her fans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In October 2010, Rowling was named the "Most Influential Woman in Britain" by leading magazine editors.<sup id="cite_ref-htanna_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-htanna-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> She has supported charities, including <a href="/wiki/Comic_Relief_(charity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Comic Relief (charity)">Comic Relief</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_Parent_Families" class="mw-redirect" title="One Parent Families">One Parent Families</a> and <a href="/wiki/Multiple_Sclerosis_Society_of_Great_Britain" title="Multiple Sclerosis Society of Great Britain">Multiple Sclerosis Society of Great Britain</a>, and launched her own charity, <a href="/wiki/Lumos_(charity)" title="Lumos (charity)">Lumos</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Name"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Name</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Life_and_career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Life and career</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Birth_and_family"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Birth and family</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Childhood"><span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Inspiration_and_mother&#39;s_death"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Inspiration and mother\'s death</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Marriage,_divorce,_and_single_parenthood"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Marriage, divorce, and single parenthood</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Harry_Potter"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Harry Potter</i></span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Harry_Potter_films"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Financial_success"><span class="tocnumber">2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Financial success</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Remarriage_and_family"><span class="tocnumber">2.8</span> <span class="toctext">Remarriage and family</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#The_Casual_Vacancy"><span class="tocnumber">2.9</span> <span class="toctext"><i>The Casual Vacancy</i></span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Cormoran_Strike"><span class="tocnumber">2.10</span> <span class="toctext">Cormoran Strike</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Subsequent_Harry_Potter_publications"><span class="tocnumber">2.11</span> <span class="toctext">Subsequent <i>Harry Potter</i> publications</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Philanthropy"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Philanthropy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Anti-poverty_and_children&#39;s_welfare"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Anti-poverty and children\'s welfare</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Multiple_sclerosis"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Multiple sclerosis</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Other_philanthropic_work"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other philanthropic work</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Influences"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Influences</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Views"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Views</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Press"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Press</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Legal_disputes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Legal disputes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Awards_and_honours"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and honours</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Publications"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Publications</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Young_adults"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Young adults</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28"><a href="#Harry_Potter_series"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.1</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Harry Potter</i> series</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-29"><a href="#Related_works"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Related works</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-30"><a href="#Short_stories"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Short stories</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Adults"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Adults</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-32"><a href="#Cormoran_Strike_series_(as_Robert_Galbraith)"><span class="tocnumber">8.2.1</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Cormoran Strike</i> series (as Robert Galbraith)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-34"><a href="#Non-fiction"><span class="tocnumber">8.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Non-fiction</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Filmography"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Filmography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>\n<p>Although she writes under the pen name J. K. Rowling, her name, before her remarriage, was Joanne Rowling. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers asked that she use two initials rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she chose <i>K</i> (for Kathleen) as the second initial of her pen name, from her paternal grandmother.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> She calls herself Jo.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Following her remarriage, she has sometimes used the name Joanne Murray when conducting personal business.<sup id="cite_ref-david_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-david-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dt_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Leveson_Inquiry" title="Leveson Inquiry">Leveson Inquiry</a> she gave evidence under the name of Joanne Kathleen Rowling<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and her entry in <i><a href="/wiki/Who%27s_Who_(UK)" title="Who&#39;s Who (UK)">Who\'s Who</a></i> lists her name also as Joanne Kathleen Rowling.<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_and_family">Birth and family</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Platform934-2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A sign reading &quot;Platform 9\xc2\xbe&quot; with half of a luggage trolley installed beneath, at the interior of King&#39;s Cross railway station." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Platform934-2014.JPG/170px-Platform934-2014.JPG" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Platform934-2014.JPG/255px-Platform934-2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Platform934-2014.JPG/340px-Platform934-2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Platform934-2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rowling\'s parents met on a train from <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King\'s Cross Station</a>. After Rowling used King\'s Cross as a gateway into the Wizarding World it became a popular tourist spot.</div></div></div>\n<p>Rowling was born to Peter James Rowling, a <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Limited" title="Rolls-Royce Limited">Rolls-Royce</a> aircraft engineer,<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and Anne Rowling (n\xc3\xa9e Volant), a science technician,<sup id="cite_ref-smithbio_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbio-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> on 31 July 1965<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Yate" title="Yate">Yate</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Gloucestershire" title="Gloucestershire">Gloucestershire</a>, England, 10 miles (16&#160;km) northeast of Bristol.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Her parents first met on a train departing from <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King\'s Cross Station</a> bound for <a href="/wiki/Arbroath" title="Arbroath">Arbroath</a> in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They married on 14 March 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> One of her maternal great-grandfathers, Dugald Campbell, was Scottish, born in <a href="/wiki/Lamlash" title="Lamlash">Lamlash</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Arran" title="Isle of Arran">Isle of Arran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Her mother\'s paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was French, and was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Croix_de_guerre_1914%E2%80%931918_(France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Croix de guerre 1914\xe2\x80\x931918 (France)">Croix de Guerre</a> for exceptional bravery in defending the village of <a href="/wiki/Courcelles-le-Comte" title="Courcelles-le-Comte">Courcelles-le-Comte</a> during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>. Rowling originally believed he had won the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9gion_d%27honneur" class="mw-redirect" title="L\xc3\xa9gion d&#39;honneur">L\xc3\xa9gion d\'honneur</a> during the war, as she said when she received it herself in 2009. She later discovered the truth when featured in an episode of the UK genealogy series <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Do_You_Think_You_Are%3F_(UK_TV_series)" title="Who Do You Think You Are? (UK TV series)">Who Do You Think You Are?</a></i>, in which she found out it was a different Louis Volant who won the Legion of Honour. When she heard his story of bravery and discovered the <i>croix de guerre</i> was for "ordinary" soldiers like her grandfather, who had been a waiter, she stated the <i>croix de guerre</i> was "better" to her than the Legion of Honour.<sup id="cite_ref-legion_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legion-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood">Childhood</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_Cottage,_Tutshill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Church_Cottage%2C_Tutshill.jpg/220px-Church_Cottage%2C_Tutshill.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Church_Cottage%2C_Tutshill.jpg/330px-Church_Cottage%2C_Tutshill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Church_Cottage%2C_Tutshill.jpg/440px-Church_Cottage%2C_Tutshill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Church_Cottage,_Tutshill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rowling\'s childhood home, <a href="/wiki/Church_Cottage,_Tutshill" title="Church Cottage, Tutshill">Church Cottage, Tutshill</a>, Gloucestershire</div></div></div>\n<p>Rowling\'s sister Dianne<sup id="cite_ref-WizardBehindPotter_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WizardBehindPotter-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old.<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The family moved to the nearby village <a href="/wiki/Winterbourne,_Gloucestershire" title="Winterbourne, Gloucestershire">Winterbourne</a> when Rowling was four.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories which she frequently read to her sister.<sup id="cite_ref-bio_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Aged nine, Rowling moved to <a href="/wiki/Church_Cottage,_Tutshill" title="Church Cottage, Tutshill">Church Cottage</a> in the Gloucestershire village of <a href="/wiki/Tutshill" title="Tutshill">Tutshill</a>, close to <a href="/wiki/Chepstow" title="Chepstow">Chepstow</a>, Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> When she was a young teenager, her great-aunt gave her a copy of <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Mitford" title="Jessica Mitford">Jessica Mitford</a>\'s autobiography, <i><a href="/wiki/Hons_and_Rebels" title="Hons and Rebels">Hons and Rebels</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-hons_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hons-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Mitford became Rowling\'s heroine, and Rowling read all of her books.<sup id="cite_ref-harryandme_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harryandme-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling has said that her teenage years were unhappy.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Her home life was complicated by her mother\'s diagnosis with <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and a strained relationship with her father, with whom she is not on speaking terms.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Rowling later said that she based the character of <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger" title="Hermione Granger">Hermione Granger</a> on herself when she was eleven.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Sean Harris, her best friend in the <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">Upper Sixth</a>, owned a turquoise <a href="/wiki/Ford_Anglia#Anglia_105E" title="Ford Anglia">Ford Anglia</a> which she says inspired a flying version that appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Like many teenagers, she became interested in pop music, listening to <a href="/wiki/The_Clash" title="The Clash">the Clash</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Smiths" title="The Smiths">the Smiths</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_Sioux" title="Siouxsie Sioux">Siouxsie Sioux</a> and adopted the look of the latter with back-combed hair and black eyeliner, a look that she would still sport when beginning university.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h4>\n<p>As a child, Rowling attended <a href="/wiki/St_Michael%27s_Primary_School" class="mw-redirect" title="St Michael&#39;s Primary School">St Michael\'s Primary School</a>, a school founded by <a href="/wiki/Abolitionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolitionist">abolitionist</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Wilberforce" title="William Wilberforce">William Wilberforce</a> and education reformer <a href="/wiki/Hannah_More" title="Hannah More">Hannah More</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Her headmaster at St Michael\'s, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the <i>Harry Potter</i> headmaster <a href="/wiki/Albus_Dumbledore" title="Albus Dumbledore">Albus Dumbledore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> She attended secondary school at <a href="/wiki/Wyedean_School_and_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Wyedean School and College">Wyedean School and College</a>, where her mother worked in the science department.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbio_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbio-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Steve Eddy, her first secondary school English teacher, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English".<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Rowling took <a href="/wiki/A-level" class="mw-redirect" title="A-level">A-levels</a> in English, French and German, achieving two As and a B<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and was <a href="/wiki/Head_Girl" class="mw-redirect" title="Head Girl">Head Girl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1982, Rowling took the entrance exams for <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a> but was not accepted<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and earned a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">BA</a> in French and <a href="/wiki/Classics" title="Classics">Classics</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fraser34_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fraser34-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-J._K._Rowling\xe2\x80\x99s_Education_Background_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J._K._Rowling\xe2\x80\x99s_Education_Background-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JK_Rowling:_10_facts_about_the_writer_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JK_Rowling:_10_facts_about_the_writer-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Martin Sorrell, a French professor at Exeter, remembers "a quietly competent student, with a denim jacket and dark hair, who, in academic terms, gave the appearance of doing what was necessary".<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Rowling recalls doing little work, preferring to read <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Dickens</a> and <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">Tolkien</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> After a year of study in Paris, Rowling graduated from Exeter in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1988, Rowling wrote a short essay about her time studying Classics titled "What was the Name of that Nymph Again? or Greek and Roman Studies Recalled"; it was published by the University of Exeter\'s journal <i>Pegasus</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Inspiration_and_mother.27s_death"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inspiration_and_mother\'s_death">Inspiration and mother\'s death</span></h3>\n<p>After working as a researcher and bilingual secretary in London for <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Rowling moved with her then boyfriend to Manchester,<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> where she worked at the Chamber of Commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, while she was on a four-hour-delayed train trip from Manchester to London, the idea for a story of a young boy attending a school of wizardry "came fully formed" into her mind.<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-loer_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loer-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When she had reached her <a href="/wiki/Clapham_Junction" title="Clapham Junction">Clapham Junction</a> flat, she began to write immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In December, Rowling\'s mother, Anne, died after ten years suffering from <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Rowling was writing <i>Harry Potter</i> at the time and had never told her mother about it.<sup id="cite_ref-dt_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Her mother\'s death heavily affected Rowling\'s writing,<sup id="cite_ref-dt_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and she channelled her own feelings of loss by writing about Harry\'s own feelings of loss in greater detail in the first book.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Marriage.2C_divorce.2C_and_single_parenthood"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage,_divorce,_and_single_parenthood">Marriage, divorce, and single parenthood</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VistadoPorto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A panned out image of city buildings." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/VistadoPorto.jpg/220px-VistadoPorto.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/VistadoPorto.jpg/330px-VistadoPorto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/VistadoPorto.jpg/440px-VistadoPorto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VistadoPorto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rowling moved to Porto to teach. In 1993, she returned to the UK accompanied by her daughter and three completed chapters of <i>Harry Potter</i> after her marriage had deteriorated.</div></div></div>\n<p>An advertisement in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> led Rowling to move to <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, Portugal, to teach <a href="/wiki/English_as_a_foreign_language" class="mw-redirect" title="English as a foreign language">English as a foreign language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WizardBehindPotter_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WizardBehindPotter-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-harryandme_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harryandme-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> She taught at night and began writing in the day while listening to <a href="/wiki/Tchaikovsky" class="mw-redirect" title="Tchaikovsky">Tchaikovsky</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_(Tchaikovsky)" title="Violin Concerto (Tchaikovsky)">Violin Concerto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> After 18 months in Porto, she met Portuguese television journalist Jorge Arantes in a bar and found they shared an interest in <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They married on 16 October 1992 and their child, Jessica Isabel Rowling Arantes (named after <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Mitford" title="Jessica Mitford">Jessica Mitford</a>), was born on 27 July 1993 in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Rowling had previously suffered a <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The couple separated on 17 November 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Biographers have suggested that Rowling suffered <a href="/wiki/Domestic_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic abuse">domestic abuse</a> during her marriage, although the extent is unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In December 1993, Rowling and her then infant daughter moved to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, Scotland, to be near Rowling\'s sister<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> with three chapters of what would become <i>Harry Potter</i> in her suitcase.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Seven years after graduating from university, Rowling saw herself as a failure.<sup id="cite_ref-twsMarE27_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twsMarE27-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Her marriage had failed, and she was jobless with a dependent child, but she described her failure as liberating and allowing her to focus on writing.<sup id="cite_ref-twsMarE27_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twsMarE27-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> During this period, Rowling was diagnosed with clinical depression and contemplated suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn23mar08_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn23mar08-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Her illness inspired the characters known as <a href="/wiki/Dementors" class="mw-redirect" title="Dementors">Dementors</a>, soul-sucking creatures introduced in the third book.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Rowling signed up for <a href="/wiki/Welfare_benefits" class="mw-redirect" title="Welfare benefits">welfare benefits</a>, describing her economic status as being "poor as it is possible to be in modern Britain, without being homeless."<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-twsMarE27_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twsMarE27-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling was left in despair after her estranged husband arrived in Scotland, seeking both her and her daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> She obtained an <a href="/wiki/Restraining_order" title="Restraining order">Order of Restraint</a>, and Arantes returned to Portugal, with Rowling filing for divorce in August 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> She began a teacher training course in August 1995 at the <a href="/wiki/Moray_House_School_of_Education" title="Moray House School of Education">Moray House School of Education</a>, at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">Edinburgh University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> after completing her first novel while living on state benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> She wrote in many caf\xc3\xa9s, especially Nicolson\'s Caf\xc3\xa9 (owned by her brother-in-law),<sup id="cite_ref-kirkbio_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kirkbio-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dole_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dole-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and the Elephant House,<sup id="cite_ref-biogonbio_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biogonbio-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> wherever she could get Jessica to fall asleep.<sup id="cite_ref-rowling-bio_25-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowling-bio-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hpandme_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hpandme-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In a 2001 <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> interview, Rowling denied the rumour that she wrote in local caf\xc3\xa9s to escape from her unheated flat, pointing out that it had heating. One of the reasons she wrote in caf\xc3\xa9s was that taking her baby out for a walk was the best way to make her fall asleep.<sup id="cite_ref-hpandme_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hpandme-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter"><i>Harry Potter</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Elephant_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/The_Elephant_House.jpg/220px-The_Elephant_House.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/The_Elephant_House.jpg/330px-The_Elephant_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/The_Elephant_House.jpg/440px-The_Elephant_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Elephant_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Elephant House, one of the caf\xc3\xa9s in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> in which Rowling wrote the first <i>Harry Potter</i> novel<sup id="cite_ref-cafe_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cafe-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1995, Rowling finished her manuscript for <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone">Harry Potter and the  Philosopher\'s Stone</a></i> on an old manual typewriter.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Upon the enthusiastic response of Bryony Evens, a reader who had been asked to review the book\'s first three chapters, the Fulham-based <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Little_Literary_Agency" title="Christopher Little Literary Agency">Christopher Little Literary Agency</a> agreed to represent Rowling in her quest for a publisher. The book was submitted to twelve publishing houses, all of which rejected the manuscript.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A year later she was finally given the green light (and a \xc2\xa31,500 advance) by editor Barry Cunningham from <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury_Publishing" title="Bloomsbury Publishing">Bloomsbury</a>, a publishing house in London.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman_26-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The decision to publish Rowling\'s book owes much to Alice Newton, the eight-year-old daughter of Bloomsbury\'s chairman, who was <a href="/wiki/Publisher%27s_reader" title="Publisher&#39;s reader">given the first chapter to review</a> by her father and immediately demanded the next.<sup id="cite_ref-Eight_year_old_saves_Potter_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eight_year_old_saves_Potter-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Although Bloomsbury agreed to publish the book, Cunningham says that he advised Rowling to get a day job, since she had little chance of making money in children\'s books.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, in 1997, Rowling received an \xc2\xa38,000 grant from the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Arts_Council" title="Scottish Arts Council">Scottish Arts Council</a> to enable her to continue writing.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 1997, Bloomsbury published <i>Philosopher\'s Stone</i> with an initial print run of 1,000 copies, 500 of which were distributed to libraries. Today, such copies are valued between \xc2\xa316,000 and \xc2\xa325,000.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Five months later, the book won its first award, a <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9_Smarties_Book_Prize" title="Nestl\xc3\xa9 Smarties Book Prize">Nestl\xc3\xa9 Smarties Book Prize</a>. In February, the novel won the <a href="/wiki/British_Book_Awards" title="British Book Awards">British Book Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/British_Children%27s_Book_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="British Children&#39;s Book of the Year">Children\'s Book of the Year</a>, and later, the Children\'s Book Award. In early 1998, an auction was held in the United States for the rights to publish the novel, and was won by <a href="/wiki/Scholastic_Corporation" title="Scholastic Corporation">Scholastic Inc.</a>, for US$105,000. Rowling said that she "nearly died" when she heard the news.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In October 1998, Scholastic published <i>Philosopher\'s Stone</i> in the US under the title of <i>Harry Potter and the Sorcerer\'s Stone</i>, a change Rowling says she now regrets and would have fought if she had been in a better position at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Red-Nose-Day-BBC-Online-chat_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Red-Nose-Day-BBC-Online-chat-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Rowling moved from her flat with the money from the Scholastic sale, into 19 Hazelbank Terrace in Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-kirkbio_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kirkbio-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Its sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i>, was published in July 1998 and again Rowling won the Smarties Prize.<sup id="cite_ref-awards_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In December 1999, the third novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>, won the Smarties Prize, making Rowling the first person to win the award three times running.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> She later withdrew the fourth <i>Harry Potter</i> novel from contention to allow other books a fair chance. In January 2000, <i>Prisoner of Azkaban</i> won the inaugural <a href="/wiki/1999_Whitbread_Awards" title="1999 Whitbread Awards">Whitbread Children\'s Book of the Year award</a>, though it lost the Book of the Year prize to <a href="/wiki/Seamus_Heaney" title="Seamus Heaney">Seamus Heaney</a>\'s translation of <i><a href="/wiki/Beowulf" title="Beowulf">Beowulf</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The fourth book, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i>, was released simultaneously in the UK and the US on 8 July 2000 and broke sales records in both countries. 372,775 copies of the book were sold in its first day in the UK, almost equalling the number <i>Prisoner of Azkaban</i> sold during its first year.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In the US, the book sold three million copies in its first 48 hours, smashing all records.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Rowling said that she had had a crisis while writing the novel and had to rewrite one chapter many times to fix a problem with the plot.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Rowling was named Author of the Year in the 2000 British Book Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-awards2_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards2-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A wait of three years occurred between the release of <i>Goblet of Fire</i> and the fifth <i>Harry Potter</i> novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i>. This gap led to press speculation that Rowling had developed <a href="/wiki/Writer%27s_block" title="Writer&#39;s block">writer\'s block</a>, speculations she denied.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Rowling later said that writing the book was a chore, that it could have been shorter, and that she ran out of time and energy as she tried to finish it.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sixth book, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i>, was released on 16 July 2005. It too broke all sales records, selling nine million copies in its first 24 hours of release.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, <i>Half-Blood Prince</i> received the <a href="/wiki/British_Book_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="British Book of the Year">Book of the Year</a> prize at the <a href="/wiki/British_Book_Awards" title="British Book Awards">British Book Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-awards_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The title of the seventh and final <i>Harry Potter</i> book was announced on 21 December 2006 as <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In February 2007 it was reported that Rowling wrote on a bust in her hotel room at the <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Hotel" title="Balmoral Hotel">Balmoral Hotel</a> in Edinburgh that she had finished the seventh book in that room on 11 January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i> was released on 21 July 2007 (0:01 <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Summer_Time" title="Western European Summer Time">BST</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and broke its predecessor\'s record as the fastest-selling book of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-sales_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> It sold 11&#160;million copies in the first day of release in the United Kingdom and United States.<sup id="cite_ref-sales_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The book\'s last chapter was one of the earliest things she wrote in the entire series.<sup id="cite_ref-last_chapter_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-last_chapter-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Potter_queue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Potter_queue.jpg/220px-Potter_queue.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Potter_queue.jpg/330px-Potter_queue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Potter_queue.jpg/440px-Potter_queue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Potter_queue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Potter queue</div></div></div>\n<p><i>Harry Potter</i> is now a global brand worth an estimated US$15&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and the last four <i>Harry Potter</i> books have consecutively set records as the fastest-selling books in history.<sup id="cite_ref-sales_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The series, totalling 4,195 pages,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> has been translated, in whole or in part, into 65 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Harry Potter</i> books have also gained recognition for sparking an interest in reading among the young at a time when children were thought to be abandoning books for computers and television,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> although it is reported that despite the huge uptake of the books, adolescent reading has continued to decline.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_films"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">Harry Potter (film series)</a></div>\n<p>In October 1998, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> purchased the film rights to the first two novels for a seven-figure sum.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> A film adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (film)">Harry Potter and the Philosopher\'s Stone</a></i> was released on 16 November 2001, and <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i> on 15 November 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-mojo_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Both films were directed by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Columbus_(filmmaker)" title="Chris Columbus (filmmaker)">Chris Columbus</a>.  The film version of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i> was released on 4 June 2004, directed by <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n">Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n</a>. The fourth film, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i>, was directed by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>, and released on 18 November 2005. The film of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i> was released on 11 July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-mojo_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a> directed, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Goldenberg" title="Michael Goldenberg">Michael Goldenberg</a> wrote the screenplay, having taken over the position from <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kloves" title="Steve Kloves">Steve Kloves</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i> was released on 15 July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> David Yates directed again, and Kloves returned to write the script.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Warner Bros. filmed the final instalment of the series, <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i>, in two segments, with <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows \xe2\x80\x93 Part 1">part one</a> being released on 19 November 2010 and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows \xe2\x80\x93 Part 2">part two</a> being released on 15 July 2011. Yates directed both films.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Warner Bros. took considerable notice of Rowling\'s desires and thoughts when drafting her contract. One of her principal stipulations was the films be shot in Britain with an all-British cast,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> which has been generally adhered to. Rowling also demanded that <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, the victor in the race to <a href="/wiki/Tie-in" title="Tie-in">tie in</a> their products to the film series, donate US$18&#160;million to the American charity <a href="/wiki/Reading_is_Fundamental" class="mw-redirect" title="Reading is Fundamental">Reading is Fundamental</a>, as well as several community charity programs.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first four, sixth, seventh, and eighth films were scripted by Steve Kloves; Rowling assisted him in the writing process, ensuring that his scripts did not contradict future books in the series.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> She told <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Severus_Snape" title="Severus Snape">Severus Snape</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Coltrane" title="Robbie Coltrane">Robbie Coltrane</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hagrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hagrid">Hagrid</a>) certain secrets about their characters before they were revealed in the books.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Radcliffe" title="Daniel Radcliffe">Daniel Radcliffe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" title="Harry Potter (character)">Harry Potter</a>) asked her if Harry died at any point in the series; Rowling answered him by saying, "You have a death scene", thereby not explicitly answering the question.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Director <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> was approached to direct the first film, but dropped out. The press has repeatedly claimed that Rowling played a role in his departure, but Rowling stated that she had no say in who directed the films and would not have vetoed Spielberg.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Rowling\'s first choice for the director had been <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python" title="Monty Python">Monty Python</a> member <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam" title="Terry Gilliam">Terry Gilliam</a>, but Warner Bros. wanted a family-friendly film and chose Columbus.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling had gained some creative control on the films, reviewing all the scripts<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> as well as acting as a producer on the final two-part instalment, <i>Deathly Hallows</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling, producers <a href="/wiki/David_Heyman" title="David Heyman">David Heyman</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Barron_(film_producer)" title="David Barron (film producer)">David Barron</a>, along with directors <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n">Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n</a> collected the Michael Balcon Award for Outstanding British Contribution to Cinema at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">British Academy Film Awards</a> in honour of the <i>Harry Potter</i> film franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2013, Warner Bros. announced an "expanded creative partnership" with Rowling, based on a planned series of films about <a href="/wiki/Newt_Scamander" class="mw-redirect" title="Newt Scamander">Newt Scamander</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them">Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them_(film)" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them (film)">first film</a>, scripted by Rowling, was released in November 2016 and is set roughly 70 years before the events of the main series.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, it was announced that the series would consist of five films, with the second scheduled for release in November 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_success">Financial success</span></h3>\n<p>In 2004, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> named Rowling as the first person to become a US-dollar billionaire by writing books,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> the second-richest female entertainer and the 1,062nd richest person in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Rowling disputed the calculations and said she had plenty of money, but was not a billionaire.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The 2016 <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Sunday Times Rich List</a></i> estimated Rowling\'s fortune at \xc2\xa3600&#160;million, ranking her as the joint 197th richest person in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-richlist_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richlist-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i>Forbes</i> removed Rowling from their rich list, claiming that her US$160&#160;million in charitable donations and the high tax rate in the UK meant she was no longer a billionaire.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In February 2013 she was assessed as the 13th most powerful woman in the United Kingdom by <i><a href="/wiki/Woman%27s_Hour" title="Woman&#39;s Hour">Woman\'s Hour</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2001, Rowling purchased a 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Estate_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Estate house">estate house</a>, <a href="/wiki/Killiechassie_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Killiechassie House">Killiechassie House</a>, on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tay" title="River Tay">River Tay</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Aberfeldy,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Aberfeldy, Scotland">Aberfeldy</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Perth_and_Kinross" title="Perth and Kinross">Perth and Kinross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Rowling also owns a \xc2\xa34.5&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> house in <a href="/wiki/Kensington" title="Kensington">Kensington</a>, west London, on a street with 24-hour security.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, Rowling was worth an estimated \xc2\xa3650&#160;million according to the <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Sunday Times Rich List</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimeswattsbrexitbrings_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimeswattsbrexitbrings-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> She was named the most highly paid author in the world with earnings of \xc2\xa372&#160;million ($95&#160;million) a year by <i>Forbes</i> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remarriage_and_family">Remarriage and family</span></h3>\n<p>On 26 December 2001, Rowling married Neil Murray (born 30 June 1971), a Scottish doctor,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> in a private ceremony at her home, <a href="/wiki/Killiechassie_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Killiechassie House">Killiechassie House</a>, near Aberfeldy.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Their son, David Gordon Rowling Murray, was born on 24 March 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after Rowling began writing <i>Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</i>, she ceased working on the novel to care for David in his early infancy.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling is a friend of <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Jane_Brown" title="Sarah Jane Brown">Sarah Brown</a>, wife of former prime minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>, whom she met when they collaborated on a charitable project. When Sarah Brown\'s son Fraser was born in 2003, Rowling was one of the first to visit her in hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-Morrison_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morrison-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Rowling\'s youngest child, daughter Mackenzie Jean Rowling Murray, to whom she dedicated <i>Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</i>, was born on 23 January 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2012, a <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">New Yorker</a></i> magazine article stated that the Rowling family lived in a seventeenth-century Edinburgh house, concealed at the front by tall <a href="/wiki/Conifer" class="mw-redirect" title="Conifer">conifer</a> hedges. Prior to October 2012, Rowling lived near the author <a href="/wiki/Ian_Rankin" title="Ian Rankin">Ian Rankin</a>, who later said she was quiet and introspective, and that she seemed in her element with children.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-macrabbit_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macrabbit-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> As of  June&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=J._K._Rowling&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the family resides in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardBT_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardBT-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Casual_Vacancy"><i>The Casual Vacancy</i></span></h3>\n<p>In July 2011, Rowling parted company with her agent, Christopher Little, moving to a new agency founded by one of his staff, Neil Blair.<sup id="cite_ref-newyorker_20-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> On 23 February 2012, his agency, the Blair Partnership, announced on its website that Rowling was set to publish a new book targeted at adults. In a press release, Rowling said that her new book would be quite different from Harry Potter. In April 2012, Little, Brown and Company announced that the book was titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Casual_Vacancy" title="The Casual Vacancy">The Casual Vacancy</a></i> and would be released on 27 September 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Rowling gave several interviews and made appearances to promote <i>The Casual Vacancy</i>, including at the London <a href="/wiki/Southbank_Centre" title="Southbank Centre">Southbank Centre</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Literature_Festival" title="Cheltenham Literature Festival">Cheltenham Literature Festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_Rose_(TV_series)" title="Charlie Rose (TV series)">Charlie Rose</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and the Lennoxlove Book Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In its first three weeks of release, <i>The Casual Vacancy</i> sold over 1 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-worldwidesales_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldwidesales-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 December 2012, it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> would be adapting <i>The Casual Vacancy</i> into <a href="/wiki/The_Casual_Vacancy_(miniseries)" title="The Casual Vacancy (miniseries)">a television drama miniseries</a>. Rowling\'s agent, Neil Blair acted as producer, through his independent production company and with Rick Senat serving as executive producer. Rowling collaborated on the adaptation, serving as an executive producer for the series. The series aired in three parts from 15 February to 1 March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cormoran_Strike">Cormoran Strike</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cormoran_Strike" title="Cormoran Strike">Cormoran Strike</a></div>\n<p>In 2007, during the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Book_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Book Festival">Edinburgh Book Festival</a>, author <a href="/wiki/Ian_Rankin" title="Ian Rankin">Ian Rankin</a> claimed that his wife spotted Rowling "scribbling away" at a detective novel in a caf\xc3\xa9.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Rankin later retracted the story, claiming it was a joke,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> but the rumour persisted, with a report in 2012 in <i>The Guardian</i> speculating that Rowling\'s next book would be a crime novel.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a> in 2005, Rowling claimed that she would much prefer to write any subsequent books under a <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonym</a>, but she conceded to <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Paxman" title="Jeremy Paxman">Jeremy Paxman</a> in 2003 that if she did, the press would probably "find out in seconds".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2013, <a href="/wiki/Little_Brown" class="mw-redirect" title="Little Brown">Little Brown</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cuckoo%27s_Calling" title="The Cuckoo&#39;s Calling">The Cuckoo\'s Calling</a></i>, the purported <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9but_novel" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9but novel">d\xc3\xa9but novel</a> of author Robert Galbraith, whom the publisher described as "a former plainclothes <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Police" title="Royal Military Police">Royal Military Police</a> investigator who had left in 2003 to work in the civilian security industry".<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The novel, a <a href="/wiki/Detective_story" class="mw-redirect" title="Detective story">detective story</a> in which <a href="/wiki/Private_investigator" title="Private investigator">private investigator</a> Cormoran Strike unravels the supposed suicide of a supermodel, sold 1,500 copies in hardback (although the matter was not resolved as of  21&#160;July&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=J._K._Rowling&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>; later reports stated that this number is the number of copies that were printed for the first run, while the sales total was closer to 500)<sup id="cite_ref-Abes_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abes-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and received acclaim from other crime writers<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and critics<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94a <i>Publishers Weekly</i> review called the book a "stellar debut",<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> while the <i>Library Journal</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s mystery section pronounced the novel "the debut of the month".<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/India_Knight" title="India Knight">India Knight</a>, a novelist and columnist for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a> on 9 July 2013 that she had been reading <i>The Cuckoo\'s Calling</i> and thought it was good for a <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9but_novel" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9but novel">d\xc3\xa9but novel</a>. In response, a tweeter called Jude Callegari said that the author was Rowling. Knight queried this but got no further reply.<sup id="cite_ref-standard_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-standard-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Knight notified Richard Brooks, arts editor of the <i>Sunday Times</i>, who began his own investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-standard_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-standard-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyall_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> After discovering that Rowling and Galbraith had the same agent and editor, he sent the books for linguistic analysis which found similarities, and subsequently contacted Rowling\'s agent who confirmed it was Rowling\'s pseudonym.<sup id="cite_ref-lyall_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Within days of Rowling being revealed as the author, sales of the book rose by 4,000%,<sup id="cite_ref-standard_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-standard-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and Little Brown printed another 140,000 copies to meet the increase in demand.<sup id="cite_ref-grauniad_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grauniad-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> As of  18&#160;July&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=J._K._Rowling&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, a signed copy of the first edition sold for US$4,453 (\xc2\xa32,950), while an unsold signed first-edition copy was being offered for $6,188 (\xc2\xa33,950).<sup id="cite_ref-Abes_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abes-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling said that she had enjoyed working under a pseudonym.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> On her Robert Galbraith website, Rowling explained that she took the name from one of her personal heroes, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kennedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Kennedy">Robert Kennedy</a>, and a childhood fantasy name she had invented for herself, Ella Galbraith.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Soon after the revelation, Brooks pondered whether Jude Callegari could have been Rowling as part of wider speculation that the entire affair had been a publicity stunt. Some also noted that many of the writers who had initially praised the book, such as <a href="/wiki/Alex_Gray_(author)" title="Alex Gray (author)">Alex Gray</a> or <a href="/wiki/Val_McDermid" title="Val McDermid">Val McDermid</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> were within Rowling\'s circle of acquaintances; both vociferously denied any foreknowledge of Rowling\'s authorship.<sup id="cite_ref-standard_143-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-standard-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Judith "Jude" Callegari was the best friend of the wife of Chris Gossage, a partner within Russells Solicitors, Rowling\'s legal representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-callegari_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-callegari-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Rowling released a statement saying she was disappointed and angry;<sup id="cite_ref-callegari_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-callegari-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Russells apologised for the leak, confirming it was not part of a marketing stunt and that "the disclosure was made in confidence to someone he [Gossage] trusted implicitly".<sup id="cite_ref-grauniad_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grauniad-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Russells made a donation to the <a href="/wiki/Army_Benevolent_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="Army Benevolent Fund">Soldiers\' Charity</a> on Rowling\'s behalf and reimbursed her for her legal fees.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On 26 November 2013 the Solicitors Regulation Authority (SRA) issued Gossage a written rebuke and \xc2\xa31,000 fine for breaching privacy rules.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_-_Chris_Gossage_Leak_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_-_Chris_Gossage_Leak-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 February 2014, Rowling announced that the second Cormoran Strike novel, named <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silkworm" title="The Silkworm">The Silkworm</a></i>, would be released in June 2014. It sees Strike investigating the disappearance of a writer hated by many of his old friends for insulting them in his new novel.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, Rowling stated on Galbraith\'s website that the third Cormoran Strike novel would include "an insane amount of planning, the most I have done for any book I have written so far. I have colour-coded spreadsheets so I can keep a track of where I am going."<sup id="cite_ref-About_Robert_Galbraith_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Robert_Galbraith-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On 24 April 2015, Rowling announced that work on the third book was completed. Titled <i><a href="/wiki/Career_of_Evil" title="Career of Evil">Career of Evil</a></i>, it was released on 20 October 2015 in the United States, and on 22 October 2015 in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Release_Date_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Release_Date-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> released a <i><a href="/wiki/Cormoran_Strike_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cormoran Strike (TV series)">Cormoran Strike</a></i> television series, starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Burke_(actor)" title="Tom Burke (actor)">Tom Burke</a> as <a href="/wiki/Cormoran_Strike" title="Cormoran Strike">Cormoran Strike</a>, it was picked up by <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> for distribution in the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2017, Rowling revealed the fourth novel\'s title via Twitter in a game of "Hangman" with her followers. After many failed attempts, followers finally guessed correctly. Rowling confirmed that the next novel\'s title is <i><a href="/wiki/Lethal_White_(novel)" title="Lethal White (novel)">Lethal White</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> While intended for a 2017 release, Rowling revealed on Twitter the book was taking longer than expected and would be the longest book in the series thus far.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsequent_Harry_Potter_publications">Subsequent <i>Harry Potter</i> publications</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the material written for <a href="/wiki/Comic_Relief" title="Comic Relief">Comic Relief</a> and other charities, see <a href="#Philanthropy"> \xc2\xa7&#160;Philanthropy</a>.</div>\n<p>Rowling has said it is unlikely she will write any more books in the <i>Harry Potter</i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In October 2007 she stated that her future work was unlikely to be in the fantasy genre.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> On 1 October 2010, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a>, Rowling stated a new book on the saga might happen.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, Rowling stated that she planned to write an encyclopaedia of <i>Harry Potter</i><span class="nowrap"
