style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/Wizarding_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizarding world">wizarding world</a> consisting of various unpublished material and notes.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Any profits from such a book would be given to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> During a news conference at Hollywood\'s <a href="/wiki/Kodak_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Kodak Theatre">Kodak Theatre</a> in 2007, Rowling, when asked how the encyclopaedia was coming along, said, "It\'s not coming along, and I haven\'t started writing it. I never said it was the next thing I\'d do."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> At the end of 2007, Rowling said that the encyclopaedia could take up to ten years to complete.<sup id="cite_ref-returns_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-returns-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2011, Rowling announced that future <i>Harry Potter</i> projects, and all electronic downloads, would be concentrated in a new website, called <a href="/wiki/Pottermore" title="Pottermore">Pottermore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The site includes 18,000 words of information on characters, places and objects in the <i>Harry Potter</i> universe.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2015, Rowling announced via <i>Pottermore</i> that a two-part play she had co-authored with playwrights Jack Thorne and John Tiffany, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Cursed_Child" title="Harry Potter and the Cursed Child">Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</a></i>, was the "eighth <i>Harry Potter</i> story" and that it would focus on the life of Harry Potter\'s youngest son Albus after the epilogue of <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> On 28 October 2015, the first round of tickets went on sale and sold out in several hours.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h2>\n<p>In 2000, Rowling established the Volant Charitable Trust, which uses its annual budget of \xc2\xa35.1&#160;million to combat poverty and social inequality. The fund also gives to organisations that aid children, one parent families, and multiple sclerosis research.<sup id="cite_ref-USAToday200707_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday200707-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Anti-poverty_and_children.27s_welfare"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-poverty_and_children\'s_welfare">Anti-poverty and children\'s welfare</span></h3>\n<p>Rowling, once a single parent, is now president of the charity <a href="/wiki/Gingerbread_(charity)" title="Gingerbread (charity)">Gingerbread</a> (originally One Parent Families), having become their first Ambassador in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-OPF_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OPF-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Rowling collaborated with Sarah Brown to write a book of children\'s stories to aid One Parent Families.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2001, the UK anti-poverty fundraiser <a href="/wiki/Comic_Relief_(charity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Comic Relief (charity)">Comic Relief</a> asked three best-selling British authors&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 cookery writer and TV presenter <a href="/wiki/Delia_Smith" title="Delia Smith">Delia Smith</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bridget_Jones" title="Bridget Jones">Bridget Jones</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Helen_Fielding" title="Helen Fielding">Helen Fielding</a>, and Rowling&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 to submit booklets related to their most famous works for publication.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Rowling\'s two booklets, <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them">Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Quidditch_Through_the_Ages" title="Quidditch Through the Ages">Quidditch Through the Ages</a></i>, are ostensibly facsimiles of books found in the <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts" title="Hogwarts">Hogwarts</a> library. Since going on sale in March 2001, the books have raised \xc2\xa315.7&#160;million for the fund. The \xc2\xa310.8&#160;million they have raised outside the UK have been channelled into a newly created International Fund for Children and Young People in Crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In 2002 Rowling contributed a foreword to <i>Magic</i>, an anthology of fiction published by Bloomsbury Publishing, helping to raise money for the National Council for One Parent Families.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005, Rowling and <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a> <a href="/wiki/Emma_Nicholson" class="mw-redirect" title="Emma Nicholson">Emma Nicholson</a> founded the Children\'s High Level Group (now <a href="/wiki/Lumos_(charity)" title="Lumos (charity)">Lumos</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In January 2006, Rowling went to <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> to highlight the use of caged beds in <a href="/wiki/Mental_institution" class="mw-redirect" title="Mental institution">mental institutions</a> for children.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> To further support the CHLG, Rowling auctioned one of seven handwritten and illustrated copies of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tales_of_Beedle_the_Bard" title="The Tales of Beedle the Bard">The Tales of Beedle the Bard</a></i>, a series of fairy tales referred to in <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i>. The book was purchased for \xc2\xa31.95&#160;million by on-line bookseller <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> on 13 December 2007, becoming the most expensive modern book ever sold at auction.<sup id="cite_ref-fetches_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fetches-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fetches_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fetches-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Rowling gave away the remaining six copies to those who have a close connection with the <i>Harry Potter</i> books.<sup id="cite_ref-fetches_181-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fetches-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Rowling agreed to publish the book with the proceeds going to Lumos.<sup id="cite_ref-macrabbit_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-macrabbit-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On 1 June 2010 (<a href="/wiki/International_Children%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="International Children&#39;s Day">International Children\'s Day</a>), Lumos launched an annual initiative \xe2\x80\x93 <i>Light a Birthday Candle for Lumos</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013, Rowling handed over all earnings from the sale of <i>The Tales of Beedle the Bard</i>, totalling nearly \xc2\xa319&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2012, Rowling was featured at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony</a> in London where she read a few lines from <a href="/wiki/J._M._Barrie" title="J. M. Barrie">J. M. Barrie</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan" title="Peter Pan">Peter Pan</a></i> as part of a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital_for_Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children">Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children</a>. An inflatable representation of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Voldemort" title="Lord Voldemort">Lord Voldemort</a> and other children\'s literary characters accompanied her reading.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiple_sclerosis">Multiple sclerosis</span></h3>\n<p>Rowling has contributed money and support for research and treatment of <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>, from which her mother suffered before her death in 1990. In 2006, Rowling contributed a substantial sum toward the creation of a new Centre for Regenerative Medicine at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh University">Edinburgh University</a>, later named the Anne Rowling Regenerative Neurology Clinic.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 she donated a further \xc2\xa310&#160;million to the centre.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> For reasons unknown, Scotland, Rowling\'s country of adoption, has the highest rate of multiple sclerosis in the world. In 2003, Rowling took part in a campaign to establish a national standard of care for MS sufferers.<sup id="cite_ref-MSSS_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSSS-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In April 2009, she announced that she was withdrawing her support for <a href="/wiki/Multiple_Sclerosis_Society_of_Great_Britain" title="Multiple Sclerosis Society of Great Britain">Multiple Sclerosis Society</a> Scotland, citing her inability to resolve an ongoing feud between the organisation\'s northern and southern branches that had sapped morale and led to several resignations.<sup id="cite_ref-MSSS_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSSS-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_philanthropic_work">Other philanthropic work</span></h3>\n<p>In May 2008, bookseller <a href="/wiki/Waterstones" title="Waterstones">Waterstones</a> asked Rowling and 12 other writers (<a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Faulks" title="Sebastian Faulks">Sebastian Faulks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doris_Lessing" title="Doris Lessing">Doris Lessing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Appignanesi" title="Lisa Appignanesi">Lisa Appignanesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Atwood" title="Margaret Atwood">Margaret Atwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Child" title="Lauren Child">Lauren Child</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ford" title="Richard Ford">Richard Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman">Neil Gaiman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Hornby" title="Nick Hornby">Nick Hornby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rosen" title="Michael Rosen">Michael Rosen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Axel_Scheffler" title="Axel Scheffler">Axel Scheffler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Stoppard" title="Tom Stoppard">Tom Stoppard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irvine_Welsh" title="Irvine Welsh">Irvine Welsh</a>) to compose a short piece of their own choosing on a single <a href="/wiki/ISO_216" title="ISO 216">A5</a> card, which would then be sold at auction in aid of the charities Dyslexia Action and English <a href="/wiki/International_PEN" class="mw-redirect" title="International PEN">PEN</a>. Rowling\'s contribution was an 800-word <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_prequel" title="Harry Potter prequel"><i>Harry Potter</i> prequel</a> that concerns Harry\'s father, <a href="/wiki/James_Potter_(character)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Potter (character)">James Potter</a>, and godfather, <a href="/wiki/Sirius_Black" class="mw-redirect" title="Sirius Black">Sirius Black</a>, and takes place three years before Harry was born. The cards were collated and sold for charity in book form in August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 and 2 August 2006, she read alongside <a href="/wiki/Stephen_King" title="Stephen King">Stephen King</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Irving" title="John Irving">John Irving</a> at <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a> in New York City. Profits from the event were donated to the Haven Foundation, a charity that aids artists and performers left uninsurable and unable to work, and the medical NGO <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="M\xc3\xa9decins Sans Fronti\xc3\xa8res">M\xc3\xa9decins Sans Fronti\xc3\xa8res</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In May 2007, Rowling pledged a donation reported as over \xc2\xa3250,000 to a reward fund started by the tabloid <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World" title="News of the World">News of the World</a></i> for the safe return of a young British girl, <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Madeleine_McCann" title="Disappearance of Madeleine McCann">Madeleine McCann</a>, who disappeared in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Rowling, along with <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Greenspan" title="Alan Greenspan">Alan Greenspan</a>, wrote an introduction to a collection of Gordon Brown\'s speeches, the proceeds of which were donated to the Jennifer Brown Research Laboratory.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> After her exposure as the true author of <i>The Cuckoo\'s Calling</i> led a massive increase in sales, Rowling announced she would donate all her royalties to the <a href="/wiki/Army_Benevolent_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="Army Benevolent Fund">Army Benevolent Fund</a>, claiming she had always intended to, but never expected the book to be a best-seller.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling is a member of both English PEN and Scottish PEN.  She was one of 50 authors to contribute to First Editions, Second Thoughts, a charity auction for English PEN.  Each author hand annotated a first edition copy of one of their books:  In Rowling\'s case, <i>Harry Potter and the Philosopher\'s Stone</i>. The book was the highest selling lot of the event and fetched \xc2\xa3150,000 ($228,600).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling is a supporter of <a href="/wiki/The_Shannon_Trust" title="The Shannon Trust">The Shannon Trust</a>, which runs the Toe by Toe Reading Plan and the Shannon Reading Plan in prisons across Britain, helping and giving tutoring to prisoners who cannot read.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_influences_and_analogues" title="Harry Potter influences and analogues">Harry Potter influences and analogues</a></div>\n<p>Rowling has named communist and <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a> activist <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Mitford" title="Jessica Mitford">Jessica Mitford</a> as her "most influential writer" saying, "Jessica Mitford has been my heroine since I was 14 years old, when I overheard my formidable great-aunt discussing how Mitford had run away at the age of 19 to fight with the Reds in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>", and claims what inspired her about Mitford was that she was "incurably and instinctively rebellious, brave, adventurous, funny and irreverent, she liked nothing better than a good fight, preferably against a pompous and hypocritical target".<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Rowling has described <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a> as her favourite author,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> calling <i><a href="/wiki/Emma_(novel)" title="Emma (novel)">Emma</a></i> her favourite book in <i><a href="/wiki/O,_The_Oprah_Magazine" title="O, The Oprah Magazine">O, The Oprah Magazine</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> As a child, Rowling has said her early influences included <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion,_The_Witch_and_The_Wardrobe" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lion, The Witch and The Wardrobe">The Lion, The Witch and The Wardrobe</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/C.S._Lewis" class="mw-redirect" title="C.S. Lewis">C.S. Lewis</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_White_Horse" title="The Little White Horse">The Little White Horse</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Goudge" title="Elizabeth Goudge">Elizabeth Goudge</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Manxmouse" title="Manxmouse">Manxmouse</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gallico" title="Paul Gallico">Paul Gallico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Views">Views</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_J._K._Rowling" class="mw-redirect" title="Politics of J. K. Rowling">Politics of J. K. Rowling</a></div>\n<p>Rowling is known for her <a href="/wiki/Centre-left_politics" title="Centre-left politics">centre-left</a> political views. In September 2008, on the eve of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour Party Conference">Labour Party Conference</a>, Rowling announced that she had donated <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>1&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>, and publicly endorsed Labour Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> over <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> challenger <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, praising Labour\'s policies on child poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Rowling is a close friend of <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Brown_(spouse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarah Brown (spouse)">Sarah Brown</a>, wife of Gordon Brown, whom she met when they collaborated on a charitable project for One Parent Families.<sup id="cite_ref-Morrison_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morrison-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling discussed the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 United States presidential election</a> with the Spanish-language newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El Pa\xc3\xads">El Pa\xc3\xads</a></i> in February 2008, stating that the election would have a profound effect on the rest of the world. She also said that <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> would be "extraordinary" in the White House. In the same interview, Rowling identified <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> as her hero.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2010, Rowling published an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, in which she criticised Cameron\'s plan to encourage married couples to stay together by offering them a \xc2\xa3150 annual tax credit: "Nobody who has ever experienced the reality of poverty could say \'it\'s not the money, it\'s the message\'. When your flat has been broken into, and you cannot afford a locksmith, it is the money. When you are two pence short of a tin of baked beans, and your child is hungry, it is the money. When you find yourself contemplating shoplifting to get nappies, it is the money."<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a resident of Scotland, Rowling was eligible to vote in the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">referendum on Scottish independence</a>, and campaigned for the  "No" vote.<sup id="cite_ref-shelley_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shelley-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> She donated \xc2\xa31&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/Better_Together_(campaign)" title="Better Together (campaign)">Better Together</a> anti-independence campaign (run by her former neighbour <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Darling" title="Alistair Darling">Alistair Darling</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-GuardBT_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardBT-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> the largest donation it had received at the time. In a blog post, Rowling explained that an open letter from Scottish medical professionals raised problems with First Minister <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a>\'s plans for a common research funding.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardBT_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardBT-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Rowling compared some Scottish Nationalists with the <a href="/wiki/Death_Eaters" class="mw-redirect" title="Death Eaters">Death Eaters</a>, characters from <i>Harry Potter</i> who are scornful of those without pure blood.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 October 2015 a letter was published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> signed by Rowling (along with over 150 other figures from arts and politics) opposing the cultural boycott of Israel, and announcing the creation of a network for dialogue, called Culture for Coexistence.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Rowling later explained her position in more detail, saying that although she opposed most of <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>\'s actions she did not think the cultural boycott would bring about the removal of Israel\'s leader or help improve the situation in Israel and Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2016, Rowling campaigned against the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">Referendum to leave the European Union</a>, stating on her website that, "I\'m the mongrel product of this European continent and I\'m an internationalist. I was raised by a Francophile mother whose family was proud of their part-French heritage ... My values are not contained or proscribed by borders. The absence of a visa when I cross the channel has symbolic value to me. I might not be in my house, but I\'m still in my hometown."<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling has been critical of <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Leader of the Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party Leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>, accusing Corbyn of tolerating anti-semitic behavior within the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour Party of the United Kingdom">Labour Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religious_debates_over_the_Harry_Potter_series" title="Religious debates over the Harry Potter series">Religious debates over the Harry Potter series</a></div>\n<p>Over the years, some religious people, particularly Christians, have decried Rowling\'s books for supposedly promoting witchcraft. Rowling identifies as a Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-conference_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conference-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> She once said, "I believe in God, not magic."<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Early on she felt that if readers knew of her Christian beliefs they would be able to predict her plot line.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, Rowling described having been brought up in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>. She said she was the only one in her family who regularly went to church. As a student she became annoyed at the "smugness of religious people" and worshipped less often. Later, she started to attend a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> congregation at the time she was writing <i>Harry Potter</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Her eldest daughter, Jessica, was baptised there.<sup id="cite_ref-conference_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conference-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a 2006 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Tatler_(1901)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tatler (1901)">Tatler</a></i> magazine, Rowling noted that, "like <a href="/wiki/Graham_Greene" title="Graham Greene">Graham Greene</a>, my faith is sometimes about if my faith will return. It\'s important to me."<sup id="cite_ref-dt_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> She has said that she has struggled with doubt, that she believes in an afterlife,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and that her faith plays a part in her books.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In a 2012 radio interview, she said that she was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Scottish Episcopal Church</a>, a province of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-20120927_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-20120927-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, following the <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Same-sex marriage in the Republic of Ireland">referendum on same-sex marriage in Ireland</a>, Rowling joked that if Ireland legalised same-sex marriage, Dumbledore and <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a> could get married there.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Westboro_Baptist_Church" title="Westboro Baptist Church">Westboro Baptist Church</a>, in response, stated that if the two got married, they would picket. Rowling responded by saying "Alas, the sheer awesomeness of such a union in such a place would blow your tiny bigoted minds out of your thick sloping skulls."<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press">Press</span></h3>\n<p>Rowling has had a difficult relationship with the press. She admits to being "thin-skinned" and dislikes the fickle nature of reporting. Rowling disputes her reputation as a recluse who hates to be interviewed.<sup id="cite_ref-Treneman_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Treneman-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 2011, Rowling had taken more than 50 actions against the press.<sup id="cite_ref-holiday_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holiday-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, the Press Complaints Commission upheld a complaint by Rowling over a series of unauthorised photographs of her with her daughter on the beach in <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> published in <i><a href="/wiki/OK!" title="OK!">OK!</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Rowling\'s young son, David, assisted by Rowling and her husband, lost a court fight to ban publication of a photograph of him. The photo, taken by a photographer using a long-range lens, was subsequently published in a <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday Express">Sunday Express</a></i> article featuring Rowling\'s family life and motherhood.<sup id="cite_ref-david_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-david-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The judgement was overturned in David\'s favour in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rowling particularly dislikes the British tabloid the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i>, which has conducted interviews with her estranged ex-husband. As one journalist noted, "Harry\'s <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Dursley" class="mw-redirect" title="Vernon Dursley">Uncle Vernon</a> is a grotesque philistine of violent tendencies and remarkably little brain. It is not difficult to guess which newspaper Rowling gives him to read [in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Goblet of Fire</a></i>]."<sup id="cite_ref-vernon_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vernon-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> As of  January&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=J._K._Rowling&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, she was seeking damages from the <i>Mail</i> for libel over an article about her time as a single mother.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Some have speculated that Rowling\'s fraught relationship with the press was the inspiration behind the character <a href="/wiki/Rita_Skeeter" class="mw-redirect" title="Rita Skeeter">Rita Skeeter</a>, a gossipy celebrity journalist who first appears in <i>Goblet of Fire</i>, but Rowling noted in 2000 that the character predates her rise to fame.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2011, Rowling was named a "core participant" in the <a href="/wiki/Leveson_Inquiry" title="Leveson Inquiry">Leveson Inquiry</a> into the culture, practices and ethics of the British press, as one of dozens of celebrities who may have been the victim of <a href="/wiki/Phone_hacking" title="Phone hacking">phone hacking</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> On 24 November 2011, Rowling gave evidence before the inquiry; although she was not suspected to have been the victim of phone hacking,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> her testimony included accounts of photographers camping on her doorstep, her fianc\xc3\xa9 being duped into giving his home address to a journalist masquerading as a tax official,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> her chasing a journalist a week after giving birth,<sup id="cite_ref-holiday_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holiday-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> a journalist leaving a note inside her then-five-year-old daughter\'s schoolbag, and an attempt by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> to "blackmail" her into a photo opportunity in exchange for the return of a stolen manuscript.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn1_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Rowling claimed she had to leave her former home in <a href="/wiki/Merchiston" title="Merchiston">Merchiston</a> because of press intrusion.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn1_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012, Rowling wrote an article for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> in reaction to <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>\'s decision not to implement the full recommendations of the Leveson inquiry, saying she felt "duped and angry".<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, Rowling reaffirmed her support for "<a href="/wiki/Hacked_Off" class="mw-redirect" title="Hacked Off">Hacked Off</a>" and its campaign towards press self-regulation by co-signing with other British celebrities a declaration to "[safeguard] the press from political interference while also giving vital protection to the vulnerable."<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_disputes">Legal disputes</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Legal_disputes_over_the_Harry_Potter_series" title="Legal disputes over the Harry Potter series">Legal disputes over the Harry Potter series</a></div>\n<p>Rowling, her publishers, and <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a>, the owner of the rights to the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</a>, have taken numerous legal actions to protect their copyright. The worldwide popularity of the <i>Harry Potter</i> series has led to the appearance of a number of locally produced, unauthorised sequels and other derivative works, sparking efforts to ban or contain them.<sup id="cite_ref-yemets_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yemets-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another area of legal dispute involves a series of injunctions obtained by Rowling and her publishers to prohibit anyone from reading her books before their official release date.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The injunction drew fire from civil liberties and free speech campaigners and sparked debates over the "right to read".<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jk-rowling-crop.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Jk-rowling-crop.JPG/170px-Jk-rowling-crop.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Jk-rowling-crop.JPG/255px-Jk-rowling-crop.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Jk-rowling-crop.JPG 2x" data-file-width="297" data-file-height="446" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jk-rowling-crop.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rowling, after receiving an honorary degree from the University of Aberdeen</div></div></div>\n<p>Rowling has received honorary degrees from <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Napier_University" title="Edinburgh Napier University">Edinburgh Napier University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a> (which she attended),<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Aberdeen" title="University of Aberdeen">University of Aberdeen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, where she spoke at the 2008 commencement ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> In 2009 Rowling was made a Chevalier de la <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9gion_d%27honneur" class="mw-redirect" title="L\xc3\xa9gion d&#39;honneur">L\xc3\xa9gion d\'honneur</a> by French President <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-legion_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legion-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Rowling became an honorary Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Physicians_of_Edinburgh" title="Royal College of Physicians of Edinburgh">Royal College of Physicians of Edinburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other awards include:<sup id="cite_ref-awards_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>1997: <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9_Smarties_Book_Prize" title="Nestl\xc3\xa9 Smarties Book Prize">Nestl\xc3\xa9 Smarties Book Prize</a>, Gold Award for <i>Harry Potter and the Philosopher\'s Stone</i></li>\n<li>1998: Nestl\xc3\xa9 Smarties Book Prize, Gold Award for <i>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</i></li>\n<li>1998: <a href="/wiki/British_Children%27s_Book_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="British Children&#39;s Book of the Year">British Children\'s Book of the Year</a>, winner <i>Harry Potter and the Philosopher\'s Stone</i></li>\n<li>1999: Nestl\xc3\xa9 Smarties Book Prize, Gold Award for <i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i></li>\n<li>1999: <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Awards_Children%27s_Book_of_the_Year" title="National Book Awards Children&#39;s Book of the Year">National Book Awards Children\'s Book of the Year</a>, winner <i>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</i></li>\n<li>1999: <a href="/wiki/1999_Whitbread_Awards" title="1999 Whitbread Awards">Whitbread Children\'s Book of the Year</a>, winner <i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i></li>\n<li>2000: <a href="/wiki/British_Book_Awards" title="British Book Awards">British Book Awards</a>, Author of the Year<sup id="cite_ref-awards2_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awards2-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2000: <a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">Officer of the Order of the British Empire</a>, for services to Children\'s Literature<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2000: <a href="/wiki/Locus_Award" title="Locus Award">Locus Award</a>, winner <i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i></li>\n<li>2001: <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Novel" title="Hugo Award for Best Novel">Hugo Award for Best Novel</a>, winner <i>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</i></li>\n<li>2003: <a href="/wiki/Premio_Pr%C3%ADncipe_de_Asturias" class="mw-redirect" title="Premio Pr\xc3\xadncipe de Asturias">Premio Pr\xc3\xadncipe de Asturias</a>, Concord</li>\n<li>2003: <a href="/wiki/Bram_Stoker_Award" title="Bram Stoker Award">Bram Stoker Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bram_Stoker_Award_for_Best_Work_for_Young_Readers" title="Bram Stoker Award for Best Work for Young Readers">Best Work for Young Readers</a>, winner <i>Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</i></li>\n<li>2006: <a href="/wiki/British_Book_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="British Book of the Year">British Book of the Year</a>, winner for <i>Harry Potter and the Half Blood Prince</i></li>\n<li>2007: <a href="/wiki/Blue_Peter_Badge" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Peter Badge">Blue Peter Badge</a>, Gold</li>\n<li>2007: Named <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters" title="Barbara Walters">Barbara Walters</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters%27_10_Most_Fascinating_People" title="Barbara Walters&#39; 10 Most Fascinating People">Most Fascinating Person</a> of the year<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2008: British Book Awards, Outstanding Achievement</li>\n<li>2008: The Edinburgh Award<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>2010: <a href="/wiki/Hans_Christian_Andersen_Literature_Award" title="Hans Christian Andersen Literature Award">Hans Christian Andersen Literature Award</a>, inaugural award winner</li>\n<li>2011: <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">British Academy Film Awards</a>, Outstanding British Contribution to Cinema for the <i>Harry Potter</i> film series, shared with <a href="/wiki/David_Heyman" title="David Heyman">David Heyman</a>, cast and crew</li>\n<li>2012: <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of the City of London">Freedom of the City of London</a></li>\n<li>2012: Rowling was among the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British cultural icons</a> selected by artist Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a> to appear in a new version of his most famous artwork \xe2\x80\x93 the Beatles\' <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper&#39;s Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper\'s Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> album cover \xe2\x80\x93 to celebrate the British cultural figures of his life.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>She was appointed <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_Companions_of_Honour" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the Order of the Companions of Honour">Member of the Order of the Companions of Honour</a> (CH) in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Birthday_Honours" title="2017 Birthday Honours">2017 Birthday Honours</a> for services to literature and philanthropy.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_adults">Young adults</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_series"><i>Harry Potter</i> series</span></h4>\n<ol><li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone">Harry Potter and the Philosopher\'s Stone</a></i> (26 June 1997)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a></i> (2 July 1998)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i> (8 July 1999)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i> (8 July 2000)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i> (21 June 2003)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i> (16 July 2005)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i> (21 July 2007)</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_works">Related works</span></h4>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them">Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them</a></i> (supplement to the <i>Harry Potter</i> series) (1 March 2001)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Quidditch_Through_the_Ages" title="Quidditch Through the Ages">Quidditch Through the Ages</a></i>
